I bought the Panasonic ES-WD51-P Epiglide Ladies Wet Dry Epilator on Amazon using my husband's account because he has prime, but I wanted to review it on mine.<br />I have been looking for an alternative to shaving for quite some time but had never found anything that got results. For reference I am in my 30's and have very thick hair. In a word ITALIAN. So I had dismissed them early on. I tried Nair, and found despite horrible chemical burns the hair was still there. So I gave up..<br />Then one day I was looking for a new car... Ha, How does this play in? Well they left me alone in a room with a TV that was playing \\"The View\\", the kicker is that there were only guys working.. Anyway, they were featuring this thing I later found out has been out a while called the \\"No, No\\" I was very intrigued. So when I went home I looked it up, and it costs $250... Yikes... I did lots of research on it and it does seem like a good product but I do NOT have that kind of money to blow on hair removal. As I was watching videos and reading, girls were saying they used Epilation along side the \\"No, No\\". That is when I started looking at Epilation.<br />I researched what to look for and read reviews. I decided to go with a cordless wet/dry. Out of those the Panasonic ES-WD51-P Epiglide Ladies Wet Dry Epilator had the highest rating. So I bought it.<br />Everything I have read has mixed reviews on how much it is going to hurt your first time using it. I have had multiple surgeries, I had a 8lb 9oz child with not anesthetic. I pluck, I tweeze, I have multiple tattoos and piercings. I am not a wuss. I have never had my legs waxed but heck, the pain lasts a few minutes and you're good right? If you have had your legs waxed you will be much better prepared than the rest of us I guarantee. For those or you that haven't I will warn you, all the pain you think is nothing does not prepare you for epilation... Your results may very of course but here is my account.<br />I charged up the Panasonic ES-WD51-P Epiglide Ladies Wet Dry Epilator and then turned it on. It sounds like some horrible grinding weed whacker you are supposed to put on your legs!!??! Now you are tense and you know it is gonna hurt.<br />TIP 1~ Start by placing it somewhere there is no hair then sneak up on a hairy spot. My hair was very short in my opinion, too short for waxing but PLENTY (read too long) for epilation. I read somewhere that you should shave and then start trying to epilate the next day. Skeptical me thought that would be ridiculous the hair would be much too short. Experienced me wishes I would have listened.<br />TIP 2~ Shave the area the day before<br />So I set the roaring epilator to my foot and sneak towards the hair on my ankle... And it rips the first few hairs from my leg. To those of you who have tattoos, the pain is similar, kind of like someone is raking a razor blade across your skin. Thousands of fine electrical shocks that will cause your leg to twitch. At this point I yelp and shut it off... And my husband begins laughing...<br />TIP 3~ Only Epilate while ALONE... Having an audience just makes you more nervous.<br />So my husband taunts me as I casually turn it on every once in a while and touch it to my leg. Finally I get up, take 3 ibuprofen, and wait for it to kick in.<br />TIP 4~ If you have ibuprofen or something STRONGER, Take it..<br />When I felt the medicine had taken effect I took my Panasonic ES-WD51-P Epiglide Ladies Wet Dry Epilator to my bath tub. I ran a pretty hot tub so my legs were covered and began to soak. I read another tip that said the hot water would soften the skin and open the pores making epilation easier. Not sure about all that but being in the hot bath made me feel more relaxed so it was easier.<br />TIP 5~ Get intoa Hot Bath<br />I decided I would show my husband and I was not coming out without smooth legs. I will not kid you if you go full tilt with long hair like I did it is going to HURT. A LOT. But, after a while it did get easier and has never hurt that bad since. That was the only time I took the Panasonic ES-WD51-P Epiglide Ladies Wet Dry Epilator into the bath or shower. I was able to use it for an hour before it died. I got one whole leg and below the knee on the other. Why one hour? Because I AM apparently a wuss, I tried to go mostly slow and get all the hair. Also it was quite a pain trying to keep a hold of that thing in the tub. The Panasonic ES-WD51-P Epiglide Ladies Wet Dry Epilator is egg shaped and made of smooth hard plastic. Add soap and you may as well trow it across the tub... I think this was a gross over site by the company. Is a little patch on Silicone rubber too much to ask on something that is going to be ripping your hair out and is made to go in the tub? My toothbrush has it for crying out loud.<br />When I got out of the tub I wanted to continue, but this model will only function cordless. I wanted to plug it in and use it corded but even fully charged this unit will not turn on if the plug is in. Another Con. So with my mostly epilated legs, I went to bed.<br />TIP 6~ Try to epilate at night, easier to go to bed and heal during the night.<br />When I awoke I noticed I had an awful lot of stubble like the hairs were broken vs pulled. As I used the epilator I noticed I had a habit of going really fast when it really hurt. If you find yourself doing this.. Go ahead... Once you get that first time over (even if you think you broke more than plucked) it is a cake walk after that. When you do a new spot it will still hurt but you mind knows you can do it. Since that first day I have ran my Panasonic ES-WD51-P Epiglide Ladies Wet Dry Epilator almost every day. Did the first two, skipped one, did two, skipped one. I still have a \\"stubbly\\" feeling to my legs but no more so than shaving. There is a lot of bare patches I would not have with shaving. This feeling stays longer than if I had shaved as well. I think that with constant love I will end up with smooth legs that last longer than shaving.<br />TIP 7~ Epilate every day if you can for the first week. You will continue to get hairs you missed and the regrowth of the broken hairs without the pain of fighting the forest.<br />This is why I think shaving the day before would have made it easier. You would not have gotten all the hairs at once and may have been much easier (read less painful)<br />On my last day off I ventured to my armpits. I don't know if they were just less painful because it is tougher skin or I am just used to it now but the arm pits were not that bad.<br />TIP 8~ DO NOT put deodorant on after epilating your armpits! I did not even bother trying the foil shaver. I am avoiding shaving, it would defeat what I am trying to accomplish epilating. It also came with a \\"beginner's\\" epilator guard. I tried it a little but didn't seem to do anything but draw out the pain, I just wanted it over with!<br />I did try to do the bikini area, while not as painful as the legs, very awkward to try and get what you wanted while avoiding what you didn't. As for between the legs... again not as painful but you must keep the skin tight. Even then I had some bleeding and will not be doing that again.<br /><br />Final thoughts on the Panasonic ES-WD51-P Epiglide Ladies Wet Dry Epilator<br /><br />For first timers having the choice between wet/ dry is nice, this epilator does have it's draw backs. Handle design is very slippery and you can only use it cordless. If you can tough it out through the first time you will be rewarded.<br />Stay Strong Ladies!! And Guys too =P<br /><br />Edit (2-15-12):<br /><br />I have since had to stop using the Panasonic ES-WD51-P Epiglide Ladies Wet Dry Epilator on my legs. I still use it for my underarms, but it was wreaking havoc on my legs. Everyone keeps talking about \\"ingrown hairs\\" in my experience this meant that I would get bumps where the hair would get balled up inside the follicle and not be able to escape. Little did I know there is another type... Hairs were growing through the top layers of my skin in such a way that my legs looked hairy. Upon further inspection you could tell that the hairs were under the skin and that is why the epilator could not reach them. After a month of shaving and exfoliation they are just now starting to be normal again. This is a great shame. I normally have dry skin and I think this played a big role in this side effect.ld not have with shaving. This feeling stays longer than if I had shaved as well. I think that with constant love I will end up with smooth legs that last longer than shaving. TIP 7~ Epilate every day if you can for the first week. You will continue to get hairs you missed and the regrowth of the broken hairs without the pain of fighting the forest. This is why I think shaving the day before would have made it easier. You would not have gotten all the hairs at once and may have been much easier (read less painful) On my last day off I ventured to my armpits. The Panasonic ES-WD51-P Epiglide Ladies Wet Dry Epilator does come with a trimmer/ shaver. I tried the trimmer and it is a cheap piece of junk. I did not even bother trying the foil shaver. I tried it a little but didn't seem to do anything but draw out the pain, I just wanted it over with! A steady red light means it is still charging, while a blinking light means it is full. Which means that after you tough it out for the first time, it won't be that bad as long as you keep up with it.<br />3- I'm not seeing this one. they ALL take a while. It's not like waxing, there is no way to grab ALL the hairs on a pass. You might as well put on some tunes & space out, while you make slow circles on your legs for a while. It'll happen. As to the breaking of hairs, I would suggest that is not accurate. Your hair grows at different rates. The device can only get hairs of a certain length. I suspect that people who think they are feeling broken hairs, are instead seeing the small hairs stuck on the device head which WERE successfully pulled, & THEN they're running their hands over their legs & feeling the stubble of the hairs that were too short to catch. If the mechanism is successfully pulling hair, then it's not breaking it. You're just feelign the hairs that are still too short.<br />4- ladies...EXFOLIATE! Al those science shows talk about what an amazing thing the skin is - tough & durable. Meanwhile, hairs are fairly delicate until they have been exposed to air. when you pull a hair, you destroy the path new growth would have traveled. It starts growing out & hits the wall, literally. Give it some help. At the end of your bath or shower, when your skin is saturated, use a loofah or something to scrub your legs, & afterward use Buddha Butter or lotion or something. I predict less trouble with ingrown hairs.<br /><br />I am entirely pleased with this. It is so quiet! It holds a charge a very long time & consistently. The Emjoi used AA batteries & started out with a high & efficient whir, then drooped in power to a pathetic whine. With this, I've done both legs thoroughly with no loss of power, then I just plug it back in. I did try it in the bath, in water, & that was lame, but it's more convenient anyway to do it dry. I suspect the whole wet/dry thing is just marketing, trying to be all things to all people.<br /><br />I would buy this again & would give it as a gift, even. the extras are unneeded tho.

  270. I am new to the epilation game. I heard about it many years ago, but it wasn't until last summer that I acquired my first epilator: a Braun model. That particular model only had 24 heads and a narrow epilation area, so I decided to bop around online to find a wider head to speed up the process of pulling out the hair on my legs. As you can most likely determine, I settled on the Panasonic ES-ED51-P Wet/Dry Epilator. After using this for a few months, I have come to a mixed conclusion.<br /><br />Construction<br /><br />The Panasonic ES-WD51-P (henceforth abbreviated as the PES) is a relatively lightweight epilator with interchangeable heads designed to manage your epilation needs. Since the product description elaborates on the components of the epilator, I won't get into the nitty-gritty, but I will point out:<br /><br />General<br /><br />• The razor recharges quickly and the battery does last a long while. After using it a few times, the maintenance epilations use so little of the battery power that I generally only need to recharge it for 20 minutes, if that. Unfortunately, as others have indicated, you cannot use the razor while it is charging, which I understand since this is a wet/dry model.<br /><br />• Changing the heads is easy and takes only a few seconds to remove, install, and use.<br /><br />Wide Epilation Head<br /><br />• Works best against flat surfaces; any type of curve/bump and it will miss the hair.<br /><br />Detail Epilation Head<br /><br />• Is ideal for facial hair; the small opening for the tweezer heads is slightly awkward in its placement, limiting the practical use on delicate areas.<br /><br />Razor Head<br /><br />• Does not shave close to the skin; is a nice inclusion with the epilator, but personally, I rarely use it. Works better if used in the shower.<br /><br />Ok Stacy, But How Does It Work?<br /><br />After charging the PES I eagerly fired up the unit to use for my legs. Since I hadn't epilated my legs in a while, the hair was fairly long and the PES was not as efficient in plucking it. Maintenance epilation goes better, but I quickly learned that the unit best functions when your body hair is only a few days growth. If your legs are reminiscent of Sasquatch, you may have difficulty on the first use.<br /><br />That being said, the wide epilation head is great in relation to the amount of skin it covers in a pass. Unfortunately, the tweezers rotate very slowly on the PES. It spins quickly enough to pluck hairs, but the slow speed of the head means the hairs are pulled slower, which results in this PES hurting more than my old Braun epilator. This is especially obvious when using the unit to remove hairs from &#34;thin-skinned&#34; areas; hair around the ankles results in an &#34;ouch&#34;! The good news is that the pain is momentary; other areas I barely felt. For what I did feel, it was no worse than a light pinch.<br /><br />In terms of hair removal the PES is good, but not great. It will take several passes to remove all of the hair from a patch of skin, but with the wider head especially, you can generally epilate both legs within a half hour or less. If you are just touching up those areas that seem to grow back overnight, you will spend less than ten minutes with the PES. I have found that the best method for me is similar to painting a room: the PES functions as the roller and covers large areas, while my Braun is like the paintbrush and is used for edges and detail work.<br /><br />Finally, I found the PES to be less effective if you use the unit in the shower. While it is recommended that your skin be clean for the best results, it seemed to me that the PES was not &#34;grabbing&#34; onto the hairs when my legs were wet and was making the whole epilation process take much longer. After a few tries in the shower I gave up and stick to dry removal only. One tip that I gleaned, however: if your skin is warm from the shower the hair removal is slightly less painful.<br /><br/>Overall<br /><br />In the end the Panasonic ES-WD51-P is a decent epilator, but could really use an RPM boost. The extra heads are a nice touch, and the width of the &#34;primary&#34; tweezer head makes for less time spent epilating. That being said, I really do not see the benefits of using this unit in the shower (unless you are shaving). Yes, there is a bit of pain involved due to the slow rotation speed of the epilator heads, but after a while you become accustomed to it. If you are worried that epilating your legs will be painful, it is not that bad, and as mentioned prior, is no worse that a pinch.<br /><br />The PES is a handy unit that does its job without too many issues. Just remember to stay on top of your hair removal so that the hair doesn't get too long for the PES, and in no time you will have smooth, sexy legs (and bikini and underarm areas) to show off in the warm days of summer. While I feel that the unit should be a bit cheaper, the portable nature of the PES means that you have the freedom to strike whatever poses that you need to get rid of hair, and thus paying that bit extra is pretty much worth it./>Overall<br /><br />In the end the Panasonic ES-WD51-P is a decent epilator, but could really use an RPM boost. The extra heads are a nice touch, and the width of the &#34;primary&#34; tweezer head makes for less time spent epilating. That being said, I really do not see the benefits of using this unit in the shower (unless you are shaving). Yes, there is a bit of pain involved due to the slow rotation speed of the epilator heads, but after a while you become accustomed to it. If you are worried that epilating your legs will be painful, it is not that bad, and as mentioned prior, is no worse that a pinch.<br /><br />The PES is a handy unit that does its job without too many issues. Just remember to stay on top of your hair removal so that the hair doesn't get too long for the PES, and in no time you will have smooth, sexy legs (and bikini and underarm areas) to show off in the warm days of summer. This is very useful for sensitive areas and getting used to epilating as well as areas that have a lot of hair and smaller regions like the underarms and bikini area (see advice below). This epilator charges fast and lasts a long time on a charge. You cannot use it while plugged in, but now that I've used one I don't feel like I would need to use it while plugged in. Plus, the cord could easily get in the way if using while plugged in. The next attachment exposes all of the tweezers, but elevates them slightly so that you aren't getting every last little tiny hair at once (again, great for the first pass when you have a lot of hair, or for beginners getting used to the epilator). Finally, it has a shaver head, which does work and cuts close to the skin for a smooth finish. Even without any attachments, the epilator works amazing and has never tugged at my skin, only tugs out the hair. Overall- I would buy this epilator again. I've shown it to my sister and she was sold on it and is looking to buy the same one.<br /><br />EPILATING (the experience): Ouch. There is no way around it, tugging hair out of your skin is painful. It feels like constant tiny electric shocks. The tugging feels akin to the quick sensation you get when you nick your skin when shaving (not the pain of it, but the tug against the skin). I was actually scared of the epilator when I first turned it on, so my husband tried it on the back of his hand. He immediately thrust it back at me and said it was worse than a tattoo. I think he was exaggerating, and he has hair that is longer than the recommended length for epilating, but that just tells you how NOT comfortable it is. However, there is hope (see advice). I ended up knowing it was worth the pain the first time I ran it against my legs and they were completely hair free.<br /><br />REGIONS OF BODY:<br />Underarms/armpits: are surprisingly the least painful. It starts as painful and after a few seconds is just annoying.<br />Bikini: Also, uncomfortable, but tolerable. The hair here tends to be thicker, so there is more of a tug on the skin in this area. This can cause the epilator to &#34;jump&#34;. It doesn't necessarily cause more pain, but is a little disconcerting because of how much you feel each hair being plucked. It really reminds me of nicking my skin with a razor, just the snagging sensation, not the pain.<br />Lower Legs: Pretty painful. I have to take breaks. Lower legs can get little red/bruised spots when the hairs are plucked. For me, it was only the first time. For some users this continues for years.<br />Thighs: Intolerably painful. I cannot do it. Everyone I know says thighs are by far the worst.<br />DO NOT USE ON FACE: I've read this and can only assume it's good advice.<br />Arms: Have not tried, but according to my husband, it's hell.<br /><br />Compared to WAXING: You have to wait for hair to be longer to wax, so you can have more hair free days with an epilator. Plus, a one time purchase of an epilator will be much cheaper than regular waxing, even if the epilator only lasts you a couple of years. Epilating makes a painful process less painful and more drawn out. Six to one half dozen..<br /><br />Compared to SHAVING: I am obsessed with the super slick smooth feel of fresh shaved skin and that feel is due in part to the razor exfoliating your skin as it cuts hairs. After epilating, my skin has a texture to it, due to the hairs being pulled out and leaving microscopic raised regions of the top dead layer of skin. It is almost unnoticeable, but I do notice. What I do is epilate, to prevent stubble for much longer than shaving would, then I shave the next day or exfoliate. Despite there being nothing to shave, this just gives me that clean shaven feel. Epilating has me sold, because my skin is smooth when I wake up. I don't wake up withstubble anywhere, so I automatically feel cleaner.<br /><br />Compared to CREAM HAIR REMOVERS: Cream hair removers often soften hairs more than they actually entirely remove them. They wear down the exterior of the hair shaft until it is very thin and some of them actually go away, but not many. An epilator is in my opinion, one hundred percent better than cream hair removers. It gets the root and hence, the entire hair.<br /><br />ADVICE/TIPS<br /><br />HOW TO EPILATE: Once the device is charged, push the button to start the tweezers rotating. If this is your first time, use the attachment that exposes only three tweezer heads. Apply to skin at a 90 degree angle from your body. Read the pamphlet on direction. I find it does not matter what direction I move the epilator in relation to hair growth. Hold skin taut when possible. Keep skin very dry. Do not use any lotions beforehand.<br />Use the tweezers without a head attachment/cover once you are ready to pluck every hair. You will feel more tugging, but ironically, reduced pain.<br /><br />PAIN: There are multiple ways to approach alleviating the pain of epilating. First off; take ibuprofen before attempting. I took 800mg before the first time, and was able to epilate my entire body sans thighs. Also, I realize I could probably use my husband's Dr. Numb cream (for tattoos) IF I wait for the anesthetic to sink in and then quickly rinse it off and dry my skin. The attachments help in various ways with pain; the three head attachment limits the epilating. This is crucial for getting used to the device. I also always start with this head when I am going at my underarms and bikini area. Take out some of the hair, then remove the attachment and get the rest. Holding your skin taut doesn't necessarily decrease pain, but it decreases the tugging. Make sure your hair is only a few mm long. Think a day or two without shaving. I can epilate effectively after one day of not shaving, so the epilator gets very short hairs. The shorter the hair, the less pain. If your hair is too long, the epilator will only have room to pinch the hair and pull, and then release before the hair is entirely pulled out. I've heard this is very painful and obviously ineffective. I find that when I start to dwell on what the pain &#34;feels like&#34; i.e. electric shocks, reminding myself that all that is happening is harmless hair plucking, really does relieve some pain. My friend who only epilates and has for years swears by a glass of wine. As long as you're not clumsy, a little numbing goes a long way. Finally, distractions can be good. Put on an easy to listen to, fun/funny movie. Think &#34;My Best Friend's Wedding&#34; or &#34;Failure to Launch&#34;, something that's both entertaining to listen to, but not so exciting you need to look up. I use my Netflix app on my phone and listen in the bathroom.<br /><br />Other tips:<br />Have VERY dry skin when doing this dry. Your skin will sweat when you experience pain. Even the tiniest amount can cause the epilator to drag. Have a towel on hand and thick tissues (not thin toilet paper). Regularly dry your skin and the epilator. Beware that the epilator will snag towels, so gently dry it in both directions to figure out which way snags the towel first, then just dry it off in the non-snagging direction after that. Tissues are handy to wipe out the little plucked hairs and to dry the surface of the epilator and your skin. Same as the towel, but towels can hold more moisture/take longer to dry, and tissues are cheap and you can use a ton to stay dry.<br />Bleeding can occur- from the tiny places where the hair is plucked. Blood, even the tiniest amount, is sticky, so quickly dry it off of your skin and the epilator.<br />Do NOT have any lotion or deodorant on skin. Skin should be clean, dry, and if possible, just exfoliated.<br />Exfoliate after (the next shower you take) to prevent in-grown hairs. Of all of the epilating I've done, I've only ever had one in-grownhair.<br /><br />Additional props:<br />This is GREAT to have before/during camping or a vacation. When you don't have access to a shower and a shave, it feels amazing to wake up with no stubble. Even when your stubble finally starts to grow in, it is fine and reduced (not all hair grows back at once). This is also great for busy students, moms, anyone who doesn't have a lot of time on a regular basis to spend on shaving, but who can find thirty minutes or so once a week. Even if I do a sloppy once over with the epilator, this still reduces shave time.<br /><br />Time Required: The first time I epilated, I did my legs, underarms, and bikini area. It took me four hours, because I was constantly stopping, drying my skin, cleaning the epilator, and taking a breather from the pain. The first time you epilate is necessarily going to be the most painful and most drawn out because you will have the most hair. Afterward, upkeep doesn't take long at all. Now, it takes me less time to epilate my legs than it does to apply shaving cream and shave, maybe two minutes a leg. Underarms take a few more minutes because your underarms have so many random curves, you have to go over them from multiple angles. Bikini area takes me the longest because the tugging is so noticeable that I can only do small areas at a time. I find it intense to use the epilator with no attachment on the bikini area, so I only use this after going over it with the three head attachment (so the time is extended due to multiple passes).<br /><br />In a nut shell: Get THIS epilator and start epilating! Regardless of how you incorporate it into your hair removal routine, you will find it adds convenience. Whether you are using it on occasion, before a trip, or whether you use it religiously, the purchase will be worth your while. Go for this price point. Cheaper will give you a crummy motor or tweezers that don't sit flush and won't pluck hairs. More money buys you ceramic plates that supposedly are great, butdo everything this epilator does and offers fewer attachments. I am such a price comparison shopper and hate wasting money, so you can rely on my high rating! I have no regrets and love this epilator.

  516. I have been shaving my legs for decades. I don't enjoy it - but who does? Stubble appears the next day and the process needs to be repeated over and over... So earlier this summer, I decided to investigate epilators - for my legs only. I spent way too much time reading reviews, and concluded that whether one will like it or not depends largely on pain threshold. I have a pretty high tolerance to pain, so decided to give it go. Given the range of prices, I looked for a model that had generally great reviews, but was not over the top expensive. Oh - and I wanted a reasonable design, as well! Based on reviews, cost, and looks, this Panasonic Epiglide seemed ideal. As a first-time user, I have been very happy with it. It has a number of guard caps and a shaver attachment, but don't use anything but the main epilating head. There are a number of excellent reviews about epilation already posted, so I will make only three observations from my experience. 1) It is recommended to shave and exfoliate a day (or two) before epilating; shaving seems redundant, but is actually the ONLY way to start with an even growth and eliminate persistent stubble. I did not do this the first few times - and had concluded that epilating simply could not give you smooth legs. THEN I shaved the day before - and voila, smooth legs. 2) The process is not particularly painful; rather, as other reviewers have noted, it feels more like a slight electric shock. I find it less painful than plucking my eyebrows, although admittedly, there are many more hairs to \\"pluck\\" on my legs, so the sting CAN bring a tear to you eye, even if it doesn't \\"hurt\\" per se. 3) Some reviewers have commented on a problem with ingrown hairs afterwards. I have been epilating for several months now, and have not had that problem at all. I use the epilator on dry skin (usually a day after shaving and/or exfoliating) and do not put anything (like lotion or an astringent) on my skin afterwards. There are always red bumps afterwards, but these fade in a hour or two. Overall, I have been very happy with epilation. I have not tried other epilators, so I cannot compare, but could not be more pleased with this one. It is comfortable to use and holds a charge for at least 40 min of continuous use; I recently took it on a 10 day trip and used it for several touch ups, but never had to recharge it. It is such a treat to go days without shaving! Well worth the slight \\"pain\\" of the process.

  534. I tried using an epilator way back in the eighties when they first came out. The concept was great, but the reality was that they just didn't get out all the hairs, and the ones that were pulled out often grew back as ingrown hairs. But the idea was great, and I've been considering purchasing an epilator for quite some time.<br /><br />Having recently tried and reviewed the [[ASIN:B00AN5LADI Veet Easy Wax Roll On Kit, 1 Count]], I knew I could handle the discomfort of continuous hair removal, but was hoping to find something that wouldn't require quite the same time commitment. This is it!<br /><br />This epilator is incredibly easy to use. The instruction manual it comes with carries many warnings, some of which had me a little concerned, but they basically came down to a bunch of CYAs. Every possible risk is mentioned, but I didn't have any problems using the product itself. Hairs are removed quickly and efficiently and with minimal pain. Yes, it does sting a bit at first, but I quickly adapted.<br /><br />Using this epilator is as easy as using a razor. It comes with a shaving head as well as a guard to use on the epilator head for newbies to the process. Having just come off regularly waxing, I opted to forgo the guard and didn't have any problems at all.<br /><br />The unit charges quickly and claims to hold 40 minutes of power. I needed only about 20-30 minutes to get both legs done, so I didn't test to see if the power held for a full 40 minutes, but I can say that the power was continuous and consistent for the entire time I was using the epilator. Clean up is also quite convenient with the little brush that comes included. For storage, the unit comes with a little satin bag that carries the epilator, the attachments, and even the power cord. Interestingly, an insert in the box directs users NOT to store the extra head and guard in the bag, but I think if you're not traveling with it, it's just fine. I would have preferred a more rigid case so things don't rattle around in the bag (heck, the box might have been a good container if it had not been designed to showcase the product and therefore have an open area that would require perfect repackaging every time you use it). But the storage bag is just avery minor complaint about a very good product. This was definitely a purchase that I am glad I made!<br /><br />ETA: I've been using this on my face--both my upper lip and chin, and it does an amazing job. While it misses a coarse hair here and there, it gets the finer hairs that are time-consuming to tweeze. While it made me cringe for the first few passes, it isn't any worse than waxing, but it is soooo much easier. And without the wax, I don't have to worry about breakouts that have resulted from the oil that's used to remove wax.
